< text>
They did some things well, but others were a complete failure.

< Review>
Found out about this place on the back of my Food For Less receipt and noticed the x-large 16" for 4.99 coupon or something like that, we tried it. Wait time for me was 20 mins. (I'd say that's about an average wait time) Picked it up and as far as I could tell, only one guy was running the place. The bread is sweet which was weird at first but its delicious, it was also greasy in the middle of the whole pie but not that bad. It's great pizza for being so cheap. Compared to little cesears, with this place you can feel it was made with love. Cheesy, I know.<//Review>

< Text>
they have kids meals for the kids. I'm a big horchata fan. I give it a 5 out of 10. it was good but it was too watery down. Employees very friendly and smiling. The chicken strips kids meal super delicious. The cheese quesadilla kids meal was good too. FYI the kids got their meals first. They have wooden chairs with no cushion. Presentation of the food was beautiful and delicious. My burrito was just a plate and a burrito. they need to work on the presentation on that one. Anyways free parking inside the garage next to the restaurant.  when you see the restaurant and a traffic light turn right inside it's free no valet. One important thing. Your cell phone signal will be one bar or none this garage is very big inside. So cell phone signals will be none.< /Text>

<username>ethan laden<//username><date>1597006222601< /date><Rating>5</Rating>< Text>
Food was delicious.  Everything we ordered was delicious.

Only one warning, the food I ordered (Oaxacan Mole) said it was 1/2 chicken.  When we got home with the food, there were two legs and thighs in both of our orders.

THAT IS NOT HALF A CHICKEN!

Half a chicken is traditionally leg, thigh, breast, and wing.  Now I may be ignorant of Oaxacan traditions regarding bifurcating chickens, but the menu should note this.

Great food, small complaint.< /Text>

< Text>
Just went for Taco Tuesday. It is only the bar area and surrounding tables that participate in Taco Tuesday so you would need to get there early or you're waiting. There is a 2 hours max stay time so it could be a while. The hostess was very friendly. She was a shining star to an otherwise blah dining experience. For me the carne asada and pollo were very salty. In contrast the shrimp had no flavor at all. We sat at the bar and even though we were together the bartender treated us as separate customers; which ended up with us having an extra helping of chips and salsa. Never got asked about drinks and the bartender didn't stay around long enough for me to even ask. Don't get me wrong, I understand most places are busy especially on Taco Tuesday but there were two bartenders and they both stayed on the other end of the bar so flagging someone's attention was tedious. My friend ordered tacos without all the extra condiments and both plates came out with all the extra stuff (first plate sent back due cheese which was specifically declined) Tacos were $3.50 each and there is a variety that you can choose as well as whether you want corn or flour tortillas.</Text>

<text>Since a friend recommended this place a few months back, I try to make it a point to visit any time I'm by the beach cities. The ladies are making fresh tortillas right when you walk in. The helote is ridiculous. I love their table salsa and home made chips. Great guac. The ceviche is delicious. I pretty much dream about the short rib tacos between visits. The short rib nachos with truffle beschemel are enough for two meals. You can't go wrong with the churros & ice cream. The staff is always very friendly. < review>
This isn't your average Mexican restaurant with sloppy plating and cheap margaritas. This joint has the best margarita mix in town made with fresh organic juices! If you try it and love it as much as I do, you can even buy a gallon to take home. Yea, you know you want to be the superstar party saver who brings the best margarita mix to a house party!

As for food, go for the Chile Braised Short Rib, the meat is so tender you could easily dig into it with a plastic spork! It sits on a bed of pozole which provides a nice complimentary texture to the meat.

Dessert? Churros con Chocolate won't disappoint! Dip those crispy little guys in some chocolate and scoop up some vanilla ice cream and you're in for a sweet ride. Your tastebuds will thank you!</review>

<rating>3< /rating><UserId.>102191991550028128685< /UserId.><Date>1447448038571< /Date>< text>
LA Weekly raved that Ortega has the best classic margarita. They also have a thing called a tequila university which sounds fun. Maybe I should try that next time when they have a flamenco dancer on a Friday night.

I came here to catch up with my sangria-loving friend, Jenn. I yelped around for some good sangria in our area and we decided to try this place. The atmosphere was dimly lit and the bar area was pretty crowded. We managed to find a bench against the wall with a small table in the back of the cantina. I'm sure this would have been nice if there was a flamenco dancer in the middle of the room. It was uncomfortable for us because we had to angle ourselves so we can talk to each other and not stare at the other tables in front of us.

The flower sangria on the bar menu caught my attention. The drink was sweet and very pretty but I think my friend wasn't amused because it didnt taste like the sangria she was craving for. The sangria had tons of tiny edible yellow flower pedals floating in the bottle. Everytime I took a sip I had a mouth full of them. I liked the drink, would be nice if it came with a strainer.

I was surprised how bland the guacamole was. Either that's how they make it or they don't know what good guac tastes like.

We decided to leave when the musicians came in. The music was booming and we couldn't talk. If you come here when they have live music, try to sit away from them so your ears won't be overwhelmed by their loud energy.

My first impression of this place wasn't that great but I'd like to give it another try when I'm in the area someday. Next time I'm getting margarita with something without guacamole.

Service: was slow, not that attentive
Interior Decor: very artsy-authentic, covered with dia de los muertos stuff<//text>

< Text>
Summary: Cadillac margaritas are fantastic.  Chips and salsa are tasty.  Carnitas are awesome.  Service is hit-or-miss from what I hear.  A miss for my first visit, unfortunately.  Lots of parking in the structure behind the restaurant. Prices are high, but quality is high.

I came here for the first time with a couple of buddies for lunch on a Sunday afternoon.  One of them had frequented Ortega multiple times previously.  The place was not super crowded or super empty.  We were seated immediately way in the back by the TVs showing Mission Impossible 2.  As we walked toward the table, we noticed how it got progressively darker and darker in the restaurant with some really interesting decorations and decor throughout.  Once seated, we were asked if we'd like anything to drink.  We asked for some waters while we took a look at the menu, and soon after we were delivered our first basket of chips with a couple sides of salsa.

We waited a little while for the server to come back and take our drink orders.  Two of us got the Cadillac margarita and the third got the Abuelo.  Our chips soon disappeared and we were given another basket and more salsa. We continued to consume chips and salsa until our server returned and took our order for food.  It then took a LONG time to get the food, and by that time we had gone through 4 baskets of chips and salsa and guacamole (which is alright, but not very flavorful).  Suffice it to say, we weren't very hungry by the time the food arrived.

We also ordered a second round of margaritas.  One of us got the Marigold margarita, which turned out to be pretty sour and not nearly as good as the Cadillac.  I requested a pomegranate and ginger margarita, but it was never delivered (which actually worked out better because I was feeling pretty buzzed off of the first drink with only some chips in my stomach for the day).  Now, on to the food.

I got the Tour of Tacos so as to get a good sampling for what the restaurant had to offer.  It came with a carne asada, shredded chicken, carnitas, al pastor, and shrimp taco for about $18.  It also came with rice and beans on the side, but those were consolidated with my buddy's rice and beans for his taquitos (kind of strange that they didn't separate out our portions).  The carne asada was good, but not great.  It had flavor and was pretty tender, but not as good as Tacos Por Favor in Santa Monica (which is my go-to Mexican restaurant of choice).  The chicken taco was actually really good (I'm not a big fan of chicken usually).  It appeared to be shredded white-meat chicken, which I prefer, and tasted great with excellent textures.  The carnitas were fantastic, too.  Really tender, tasty, and awesome.  The al pastor was similar to the carne asada in that it was good, but not great.  Textures were a little chewy and flavor was so so.  The shrimp taco was really good, but only had four shrimp, so it didn't really fill up as much as the other four tacos, which were much more substantial.

The beans were pretty bland, but the rice was pretty good.  I got to try some of my other buddy's carne asada burrito (with no cheese or sour cream, but with verde sauce).  It was alright.  Again, the texture of the steak was not super tender, and the burrito was indeed on the dry side.  Though, it was massive, to be sure.

The total bill came to about $130 for three of us, which is obviously a pretty expensive meal for lunch.  I will likely come again to have some more margaritas and carnitas, but I will stick to the Cadillac and the stuff that I know is good.  I will also have to be sure to not to eat so many chips, or order sooner, so as to work around the possibility of the food taking a long time to arrive.<//Text>
